    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2651720179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2651720179" />
    <a title="Andy " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11331153-andy"><img alt="Andy " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455636729p2/11331153.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2651720179?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy " href="/user/show/11331153-andy">Andy </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2651720179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2941301374068576721">The main character of this novel, Jonathan Noel just wants a quiet life, without people and drama. He's just waiting to die so he can escape this world he never asked to be in. He works a mind-numbing job as a pacing bank security guard. He once envied a homeless man with more freedom than himself, until a couple decades ago in the mid-60s when he saw him take a shit in the street. That has kept him faithful to his job and his style of life all these years -- he can avoid shitting in the street.</span>
  <span id="freeText2941301374068576721" style="display:none">The main character of this novel, Jonathan Noel just wants a quiet life, without people and drama. He's just waiting to die so he can escape this world he never asked to be in. He works a mind-numbing job as a pacing bank security guard. He once envied a homeless man with more freedom than himself, until a couple decades ago in the mid-60s when he saw him take a shit in the street. That has kept him faithful to his job and his style of life all these years -- he can avoid shitting in the street. One day a pigeon interrupts his routine, setting off a series of events that snowball and threaten to destroy his peaceful semi-existence.<br /><br />This is an existentialist novel in the vein of Camus, with the obsessive force of Poe and a touch of the alienated, nightmarish world of Kafka. The character of Jonathan Noel reminded me of Hermann Ungar's protagonist in "The Maimed" -- a man who avoids any adjustment to his routine so strictly that a wrench thrown into the works makes him believe his entire life is destroyed. The silent German expressionist film The Last Laugh (1924) also came to mind, which is about a hotel doorman getting too old for his job -- what is most similar is the impending sense of doom.<br /><br />The plot seems a bit far-fetched, but I'm sure we have all had events happen to us that make us question our life purpose, or whether our lives can continue as they have. What is most memorable about the book is the sustained tension and visiting a mind so obsessed with regularity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2941301374068576721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Bf8V6ffZmgbTA5coS0wOoiOQMku+6mkJTUDBYRtlvZKKZV9e+a4pIsHfUvkLAK13C6u9dGkhkLTEwFrTGrB9wQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PeCgkrN297uv1Ex6ocKgpCqtoTlx8mvqdksFp9SlBLiyeuolvQFEn70IiavhjgNxApYuBqY5klf/y54V1XDE6w==')})
  }

الكاتب الروسي &quot;نيكولاي غوغول&quot; (1809- 1852) من أعظم كتاب روسيا في القرن التاسع عشر، يشهد له جملة شهيرة قالها دوستو يفسكي: &quot; كلنا خرجنا من معطف غوغول&quot; قصصه مستمدة من مظاهر الحياة في بطر سبورغ ويجمع بينها المضمون العام والمغزى الاجتماعي العميق حيث تسيطر فيها موضوعة مشتركة تتمثل في التصادم بين حلم الإنسان وواقعه، واتساع الفروق الاجتماعية بين الناس البسطاء المستضعفين والأثرياء ذوي النفوذ. ولمكانة هذا الكاتب ينقل لنا الأستاذ &quot;محمد الخزاعي&quot; إلى العربية روايتين لـ &quot;غوغول&quot; هما: &quot;المعطف&quot; و&quot;الأنف&quot; منقولة عن الترجمة الانكليزية لرونالد ويلكس التي نشرتها &quot;دار بنجوين في سلسلة &quot;كلاسيكيات بنجوين&quot; في طبقها عام 1972.\nتحكي &quot;المعطف&quot; قصة رجل مسكين يدعى أكاكي أكاكيفتش، رجل يعيش آخر سوى النسخ ولو سلمت له وظيفة أخرى لما كان سيكون قادراً على إتمامها، يتعرض لسخرية من زملائه في العمل دائماً... يعيش بمعزل عن العامة.. لا يملك سوى معطفاً واحداً يحاول ترقيعه ولكن يبدو أنه لا جدوى، فيلجأ لشراء معطف جديد ثمين بالنسبة لفرد فقير مثله. تتغير حياته قليلاً... إلى أن يأتي يوم ويسرق فيه معطفه ويتغير كل شيء، يحاول أن يبلغ الشرطة وأن يتحدث لشخص مسؤول ولكن ذلك يكون بلا جدوى فيصاب بالحمى ويموت.\nأما قصة &quot;الأنف&quot; فتتحدث عن أنف فصل عن وجه صاحبه وراح يتجول كشخصية مستقلة في بطرسبورغ وبطل القصة هو يعقو بليفيتش –حلاق- قانع بعيشته. في يوم من الأيام وعند تقطيعه الخبر يجد أنفاً بين الخبز والغريب أن الأنف مألوف لديه.. إنه يخص مفتش الكليات كوفاليوف الذي تعوَد أن يحلق له أيام الأربعاء والأحد. فيخاف ويحاول التخلص منه، وبدأ يقرص جسمه ليتأكد من أنه لم يكن نائماً!!\nالروايتان كان لهما تأثير هائل على المثقفين والقراء في روسيا لدقة تركيزها وإنسانيتها العميقة وتعاطفها مع الإنسان الضعيف المسحوق. وفضحها للتراتب الطبقي في تلك الفترة من الزمن.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"7835069356994600344\" href=\"#\"           $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_59151').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/39402.Patrick_S_skind">About Patrick Süskind</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/39402.Patrick_S_skind"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1201117958p3/39402.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/39402.Patrick_S_skind">Patrick Süskind
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,943
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12138725721889324732">From 1968-1974 he studied medieval and modern history in Munich and Aix-en-Provence. In the '80s he worked as a screenwriter, for Kir Royal and Monaco Franze among others. <br/><br/>After spending the 1970s writing what he has characterized as “short unpublished prose pieces and longer un-produced screenplays”, Patrick Süskind was catapulted to fame in the 1980s by the monodrama <i>Der Kontrabass</i> (<i>The Double B</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12138725721889324732" style="display:none">From 1968-1974 he studied medieval and modern history in Munich and Aix-en-Provence. In the '80s he worked as a screenwriter, for Kir Royal and Monaco Franze among others. <br /><br />After spending the 1970s writing what he has characterized as “short unpublished prose pieces and longer un-produced screenplays”, Patrick Süskind was catapulted to fame in the 1980s by the monodrama <i>Der Kontrabass</i> (<i>The Double Bass</i>, 1981), which became an instant success and a favourite of the German stage. In 1985 his status as literary wunderkind was confirmed with the publication of the novel <i>Das Parfüm. Die Geschichte eines Mörders</i> (<i>Perfume: The Story of a Murderer</i>), which quickly topped the European best-seller list and eventually sold millions of copies worldwide.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12138725721889324732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
